S.K.Y. was instantly reminded of the time he was killed by this exact move, it was far more painful than a thousand cuts. It was as if his body and soul had been shredded into thin strands and thrown into a pot of boiling oil! That kind of pain was impossible to forget for a lifetime.

‘Kill her. I swear I’ll kill her!’ Clenching his fists, S.K.Y. trembled uncontrollably. His pupils flickered between red and black, an eerie sight.

Beside him, Taurus stared at the livestream screen, so excited he nearly burst into song on the spot. “She did it, she did it! She finally used her ultimate! The Black-Hearted Princess’ cooldown is gone!”

At those words, S.K.Y. snapped back to reality. His eyes returned to normal as he sneered coldly, “Heh… This time, she’s dead for sure!”

Forcing Yae-hime to unleash the Ancient Celestial Sword Formation was the most crucial part of their plan. They intended to use those cannon fodder players to wear down her strongest move.

“Annihilate!” At that moment, that detestable Black-Hearted Princess was finally about to release her ultimate attack.

Within the sword formation, every player was stricken with sheer terror as the claws of death pierced their bodies, flooding them with despair.

The first golden blade of essence flashed. Immediately after, golden brilliance filled the skies and space trembled violently! If what came before had felt like the apocalypse descending, this was the apocalypse arriving in full.

At least, it was the end for these players.

The swords of golden essence burst forth like a torrential storm, shredding the players’ bodies into thousands of pieces in an instant. More accurately, now they were experiencing exactly what S.K.Y. had felt. That unbearable torment of body and soul being destroyed at once, worse than death itself!

The whole process seemed to last only a second, and yet, it also felt like an eternity.

In the livestream chat, no comments appeared. It was utter silence. The viewers were all deeply shaken by the terrifying power of the sword formation, left in speechless awe. After all, nearly ten thousand players were completely annihilated in the blink of an eye by a single technique. It was beyond terrifying!

“They… they’re all dead…” Mira stared unblinking at the livestream, feeling as if a magnitude twelve earthquake had just struck her soul.

Those players were all at least level ten or above. And yet they were completely obliterated in mere moments, without even leaving corpses behind!

She had long heard that the Black-Hearted Princess possessed a terrifying ultimate move, but she never imagined it would be this terrifying.

“Until our guild reaches a certain level of strength, we must absolutely avoid crossing her. Otherwise, just one encounter could wipe us all out!”

The current livestream screen was flickering with white and gold light, making it nearly impossible to see what was happening inside. Even so, Mira could faintly make out the shadowy figure of the dark beast still trapped within the formation. That made her even more curious about what would follow during the “garbage time” phase.

Unfortunately— After exterminating all the players, the golden essence blades pierced straight through the shadow beast’s body, swiftly ending its life.

“Even that sturdy beast only survived half a second longer… The Ancient Celestial Sword Formation is truly terrifying!” Mira couldn’t help but suck in a cold breath.

Just then, the livestream feed went black. No one around the world could see what happened next.

“So tired…” In-game, Yae-hime let out a soft breath. Her face was pale, her body feeling utterly drained by the sword formation. “I can only sustain it for a few seconds at most right now.”

There was no denying it, Ancient Celestial Sword Formation was as powerful as it was draining.

“The quality of the Dragon Abyss Sword: Dragonsorch really is extraordinary. It only lost 10 points of durability.” Looking at the peculiar blade still burning with flame in her hand, Yae-hime nodded with satisfaction.

If each use broke a sword, the cost of this move would be way too high. Even with vast wealth, she wouldn’t be able to afford it. Let alone now, when she was broke.

As she looked around, Yae-hime’s eyes sparkled.Because she saw gear scattered all over the ground. Common, uncommon, and rare equipment, at least two or three thousand pieces in total.

Even though most of it was standard gear and not very valuable… With such a large amount, it still amounted to a sizable profit. What’s more, she could even enhance some of it slightly before selling to earn even more.

“Good thing most of it’s standard gear. Otherwise, my backpack and storage ring wouldn’t be able to hold it all.”

Identical equipment could be stacked in the inventory, which saved a lot of space.[1](https://re-library.com/translations/reborn-as-a-transcendent/volume-3/chapter-705-the-might-of-the-sword-formation/#easy-footnote-bottom-1-110540)　

Retracting her gaze, Yae-hime checked her mana. Only a little more than ten points remained. The sword formation had nearly drained her dry.

“Heh… And they thought I didn’t know what kind of schemes they were cooking up? Truly laughable.” She chuckled softly and pulled out Ocean’s Tears from her spatial ring, instantly restoring her mana.

At almost the same moment, violent tremors shook both the interior of the Mangrove Forest and the surrounding plains.

“Taurus, S.K.Y., let me see what you’ve got.” Yae-hime was rather fond of these two walking piggy banks.

She stabbed her sword into the ground and struck a weak pose, pretending to be exhausted, waiting for them to strike. However, before Taurus and S.K.Y. could make their move, the system notification beat them to it.[2](https://re-library.com/translations/reborn-as-a-transcendent/volume-3/chapter-705-the-might-of-the-sword-formation/#easy-footnote-bottom-2-110540)　

Ding!

+++

# 706 – Encircled on All Sides, A Lethal Checkmate!?

Upon hearing the system notification, Yae-hime immediately had a bad feeling. Considering what she had just done, it was highly likely she would receive a negative status.

You have slaughtered players wantonly within the borders of the Jade Empire.

All hostile factions within the Jade Empire have had their favorability toward you reduced by 1000.

You are now wanted across the entire nation.

Note: You were already wanted. Your PvP status has been stacked.

Your PvP status has been updated to: Blackish-Red.

Attack Power: +100%

Defense Power: -75%

Equipment Drop Penalty: Upon death, you will drop one piece of Rare or higher-grade equipment with 100% certainty.

Ways to Remove PvP Status:

Surrender voluntarily and serve a 100-day prison sentence.

Survive for six days without being captured or killed by players or NPCs.

Note 2: Your PvP status applies to both players and NPCs.

Sure enough, the system had slapped her with a negative status effect. Just as Yae-hime was about to comment, the system notification rang out once more.

Ding!

The total number of players you have killed has surpassed twenty thousand. You have acquired a temporary skill:

|Bloodthirsty Rage|   |

|---|---|

|Type|Temporary Skill|

|Attribute|None|

|Special Effect 1|While using this skill, you will become a bloodthirsty monster. The more you kill, the stronger you get!  <br>For every player killed, Attack Damage +10, Critical Damage +10, no upper limit.|

|Special Effect 2|While using this skill, your Defense is halved and Attack Speed +150%.|

|Special Effect 3|No cooldown time and no energy consumption.|

|Description|Kill one person, and you’re a murderer.  <br>Kill a hundred, and you’re a homicidal maniac.  <br>Kill a thousand, and you’re a devil.  <br>Kill ten thousand, you’re a God of Slaughter!  <br><br>Pick up your blade and revel in the massacre, my child!<br><br>(This skill only affects players.)|

Ding!

You have obtained the title: God of Slaughter.

After hearing the system notification, Yae-hime wasn’t sure whether to feel happy or sad. Because earning the Bloodthirsty Rage skill essentially meant she now possessed unmatched offensive power. Killing players would be easier than squashing ants.

The problem was, due to the PvP status and the new skill, her defense had been shredded to paper-thin levels. Just one coordinated volley, and she would be utterly annihilated.

This situation was nothing like back in the beginner village. The enemies now had stronger attacks and far more intense firepower.

At this very moment, figures surged in from every direction. It was an enormous encirclement! The number of enemies far exceeded her expectations.

‘This is bad. Even with an artifact that reduces damage, I can’t possibly survive this level of concentrated fire.’

Feeling the ground subtly trembling, Yae-hime quickly estimated the number of enemies.There were clearly more than before, and stronger as well. Could this really be… a trap with no way out?

Her face gradually turned pale, and her expression grew uneasy. Her tightly gripped sword trembled slightly in her hands.

The encirclement was closing in fast. For a moment, it looked like a tide of ants… but no, those were players, just as densely packed and relentless.

About one-fifth of them were elite players around level 20. The foundation of the Death of Love guild was truly terrifying!

“Princess, a pleasure to meet you.” From among the players nearby, a beautiful woman stepped forward. It was Vanessa from the Death of Flower guild.

“Meeting you in a place like this… what a delightful encounter. I’m a straightforward person, so I’ll get straight to the point. That purple bow of yours belongs to me. Whether you give it or not… it’s mine either way.” She casually flipped her long black hair, speaking with arrogant confidence. In her eyes, this was a sure-death situation.

No matter how capable the Black-hearted Princess might be, there was no way to turn the tide.

“Hahahaha! Black-hearted Princess, bet you didn’t see this coming!”

Before Yae-hime could respond, arrogant laughter rang out from the other side. She turned her head and saw Taurus and S.K.Y. standing together, their faces filled with unrestrained glee. They looked as if victory was already in their grasp.

“Give up. Despair. From the moment you unleashed the sword formation, the scales of victory have tilted entirely to our side!” S.K.Y. adjusted an imaginary pair of gold-rimmed glasses.

“Today, you will die a miserable death!” His voice carried unrestrained hatred, and a hint of joy. The joy of a long-awaited revenge. The grudge he had built up over this time could finally be repaid with interest.

“Heh, the gates of heaven you ignored, and now you barge into hell instead. Foolish Black-hearted Princess, you’re about to pay the price for your greed!” Taurus stood upright and raised his right hand, fingers spread as he swept them back through his hair in a pretentious display.

All the preparations laid out until now were about to bear fruit. The treasure vault he had long dreamed of was finally within reach. In that moment, he felt like he was standing at the peak of life itself, his heart and soul filled with bliss.

“Greed?” Yae-hime sheathed the Dragon Abyss Sword and stood tall, though her face remained visibly pale. She looked as if she were barely holding herself together.

‘She’s totally spent!’ Those words echoed through the minds of every player present. A few felt an odd wave of melancholy rise in their hearts.

Though the Black-hearted Princess was far from a hero, to see such a dominant force fall to ruin still stirred a sense of pity and regret. Of course, that was only a minority opinion. Most people were basking in schadenfreude.

They had long held resentment and disdain for Yae-hime’s tyrannical rule over Jade City. But more than that, it had always been fear. Now, watching this former ruler meet such a pitiful end filled them with joy.

“If one has no desire for greed, then what makes them any different from salted fish?” Yae-hime replied with a bland tone.

Vanessa let out a cold laugh. “Know how to write the word ‘poor’? That’s the price of your insatiable greed.”

Taurus nodded. “Your mistake was not having the power to protect yourself. Today, you’ll lose everything.”

“How pitiful, how laughable, how tragic, how absurd.” S.K.Y. stared at Yae-hime, who stood alone in the middle of the encirclement, the smile on his lips growing deeper.

Yae-hime remained silent, seemingly calm. She gave off the impression of a sage facing death with serenity. Aloof. Unbothered. Dignified.

At that moment, Taurus snapped his fingers, and the surrounding players all activated their livestreams. The pitch-black screens of the livestream channels flickered back to life.

The viewers who had waited patiently were met with a strange scene: a lone girl, standing like a proud snow lotus, encircled by a sea of shadowy figures.

They stared, confused. Hadn’t the Black-hearted Princess just unleashed a terrifying sword formation that wiped out every player? Why were there still so many present on the battlefield? Not only were these players still around, they seemed even stronger and more overwhelming!

Seeing everything unfold exactly as she had predicted, Mira’s lips curled into a faint smile.

“Black-hearted Princess, you’ve never died before, have you?” Taurus fixed his gaze on Yae-hime.

She still said nothing.

“Heh, seems like this will be your first time. Good. Very good! Black-hearted Princess, your first death won’t come from a monster, nor from an NPC, but by my hands—me, Taurus!”

He pointed directly at Yae-hime, proudly declaring to the world his claim to her first kill.

“Heh.” At last, Yae-hime responded. She revealed a dangerously seductive smile. Her gently parted cherry lips released words dripping with contempt. “You lot really think you’ve won, don’t you? That it’ll be easy to take me down? Seriously now, do you not even realize you’re just a bunch of vegetables waiting to be harvested?”

The moment her voice fell, silver light exploded across the scene!

+++

# 707 – It’s Here! Love’s Got Us Spinning in Circles~

Witnessing the sudden flash of silver light, everyone froze, completely unsure of how to react. Only S.K.Y. snapped back to his senses instantly and shouted in panic, “Taurus! Kill the Black-hearted Princess right now!”

A terrible premonition gripped his heart. It felt as if the claws of death had seized him by the throat. He had experienced this feeling before, and every time, it had come true. And the one who always brought him this feeling was none other than the Black-hearted Princess!

Taurus didn’t respond to S.K.Y.’s call at all. Because at that moment, his entire attention was captured by the sword in the Black-hearted Princess’ hand. His heart trembled violently. That exquisite longsword was clearly a replica of Yasa’s Sword of Eternity!

“How did you get that sword!?” Taurus cried out in shock.

But he wasn’t the only one who was stunned. Both the players and the viewers watching the livestream were equally shaken. To many, the Sword of Eternity was no stranger. They had seen it back when the Black-hearted Princess dueled Yasa. And they had been utterly captivated by its terrifying power.

But no one had expected that the sword would end up in the hands of the Black-hearted Princess!

Someone quickly pulled up the equipment rankings, and sure enough, the Sword of Eternity replica had climbed to the top spot. It was a genuine Unique-tier weapon! The moment it was confirmed, players around the globe were thrown into shock and terror!

It was supposed to be a certain-death scenario, and yet she had pulled out such a devastating trump card. The Black-hearted Princess truly was terrifying beyond belief. She was inhuman.

At that moment, many players present couldn’t help but recall the fear of being dominated by the Black-hearted Princess in the past.

“No… We’re not the ones surrounding her—she’s the one surrounding us!” One player, face pale, legs trembling, cried out in a twisted expression of despair.

Hearing this, the players nearby shuddered. Retreating thoughts began to spread through the ranks.

“Taurus! Give the order to kill her right now!” S.K.Y. urged frantically. If this continued, the morale would completely collapse. They were all going to die! No, even S.K.Y. himself would meet a miserable end right here. That future was almost certain!

“I—I got it! Everyone, launch a full-scale attack!” Taurus finally came to his senses and shouted in a panic. Unfortunately, the scene was already in complete disarray. Even though the order had been given, no one immediately followed through.

By the time the players had somewhat regained their composure and prepared to strike, a clear, melodic voice suddenly rang out.

“Absolute Space.” Everyone turned toward the sound, only to see Yae-hime plunge her sword into the ground. She had activated the third special effect of the Sword of Eternity.

This was an exclusive wide-area attack skill of the Eternity Sword replica, with a unique effect known as Terrain Collapse. As for its destructive power, that depended entirely on the wielder’s own strength!

Though Yae-hime wasn’t even at full power, the bonus from her PvP Status made her attack strength absurdly high. The blade pierced the ground as if it were stabbing into tofu, smooth and effortless.

Then, all of the erupting silver light surged directly into the earth.

In the next instant, the ground began to shake violently. Everyone was thrown off balance, and the attacks they had been preparing went flying in all directions. The battlefield plunged into utter chaos.

Their nightmare wasn’t over yet. A loud cracking sound split the air.

Viewers in the livestream watched as the ground began to split apart, and countless streams of silver light burst out like geysers, swallowing up all the players in their path. In the blink of an eye, a fifth of the players had fallen.

“No!” Taurus cried out in disbelief upon seeing the terrifying spectacle.  

“Damn it!” S.K.Y. roared with fury.

His rage was directed at both Yae-hime and Taurus. The former filled him with despair so deep it turned to fury. And the latter… did the exact same. But the two were fundamentally different.

Yae-hime was terrifying. Taurus was simply incompetent!

In less than two seconds, two major guilds had lost two-thirds of their members. The battlefield was engulfed in dust, and the air was filled with unending wails of agony. The ground around them had become a disaster zone, like it had been struck by a magnitude twelve earthquake.

The word “apocalypse” surfaced in S.K.Y.’s mind. Today marked the end of both Death of Love and Death of Flower.

Vanessa stood in complete shock. Taurus trembled all over. His pupils shrank, and his face turned pale as paper. The remaining players shared the same despair as them. Faced with this horrifying… no, this demonic presence, they could do nothing but fall into hopelessness.

Yet, what pushed that despair even further—

“Ten seconds, eleven, twelve, thirteen…”

That demon still stood in the same spot.

But now, the Sword of Eternity had been fully drawn. Both her hands gripped the hilt as violent energy continuously surged into the blade. That seemingly meaningless countdown sent chills through everyone’s bones.

The livestream fell into absolute silence. Everyone was so stunned they couldn’t utter a word. This Black-hearted Princess… she was no human. She was a monster. A humanoid world boss. Those who once doubted Yae-hime’s strength were now utterly convinced. Not only that, but an unshakable fear had been engraved in their hearts.

Many were secretly relieved. Thank goodness… they weren’t on the same server as this monster!

“Fifteen seconds. Charging complete.” At that moment, Yae-hime finished her countdown and smiled sweetly. Then she looked toward Taurus and S.K.Y. and said, “Cannon fodder should know their place.”

At those words, everyone trembled! They knew full well…that was the signal to attack. This demon was about to begin the real massacre!

‘Run. We have to get out of here now!’

Some frantically opened their game menus and clicked the logout button. Some ran for their lives. Some stood frozen, not out of confusion, but out of sheer terror that robbed them of the ability to react. But no matter how they struggled, none could escape the clutches of the demon.

“Heavenrend!” Yae-hime whispered coldly, gripping the Sword of Eternity with both hands and swinging it down in a mighty arc. This was the wide-area attack skill exclusive to the Sword of Eternity, which required fifteen seconds of charging time before activation. Its power scaled entirely with the wielder’s strength.

And the Yae-hime now, was not the same as the Yae-hime from a moment ago. Thanks to the effects of Bloodthirsty Rage, her damage against players had already broken into the six-figure range. Even the faintest wave of energy could wipe out thousands!

A flash of silver surged forth, transforming the entire world into a silver ocean. Any player caught in the wave of silver light disintegrated into dust in an instant. And for those who had managed to avoid the initial sweep? It didn’t matter.

Yae-hime spun on her heel, and the silver light transformed into a radiant ring that expanded in all directions, executing a 360-degree annihilation without blind spots!

“No!” Taurus screamed in utter despair.  

“How could this happen!” Vanessa cried out in panic.  

“Damn it!” S.K.Y. roared in fury.

It was unclear whether he cursed at Yae-hime, Taurus—or both.

But all the shouting, screaming, and cursing… was silenced in an instant by the sweeping wave of silver light. Taurus, S.K.Y., and Vanessa became a perfect demonstration of the classic trope: villains die because they talk too much.

From the moment they appeared to the moment they were completely wiped out, it had only been a few minutes. But those few minutes left an unforgettable impact, an overwhelming shock and an indescribable thrill.

At this very moment, the Black-hearted Princess was like the livestream that had suddenly gone black, seared into their eyes and etched deep within their hearts.

+++

# 708 – The Taste of Reaping Leeks, Everyone Wants a Taste of It!

At the very moment the livestream went dark, the Princess Alliance chatroom instantly erupted in excitement. Nangong Lin and the others were practically thrilled to the point of frenzy, as if injected with adrenaline.

During the first round of the stream, by the time they had received the news, the broadcast had already gone black. When the second round of the livestream resumed, they saw Princess at an absolute disadvantage, which made them extremely anxious.

However, true to her name, Princess had effortlessly reversed the tide of battle. That kind of dramatic turnaround sent them into waves of ecstasy, shouting her name like fangirls to vent their inner excitement.

Nangong Lin: Princess, number one in the world!

Mylene: No, no, my sister is number one in the universe!

Pixie: She’s way too badass. I completely surrender.

Snowy: That fight gave me chills… I’m still not over it.

Yunuen: That was even more intense than that showdown in Novice Village.

Little Fairy: Mmm, she’s so good! My legs are literally jelly right now.

Rakshasa: Princess, the best! My favorite!

Sachiel: _Hnnnnn_… So cool… my Princess is totally invincible!

---

At this moment, the invincible Princess had just finished drinking a bottle of High-Level Mana Recovery Potion.

“After making such a commotion, even though this place is far from Jade City, reinforcements will definitely be on their way. And those players watching the stream are bound to report me. Better grab the spoils quickly and get out of here.” Yae-hime looked around at the devastated land and murmured to herself.

Beneath the same sky, outside Jade City. Commander Blei led a troop of elite black-armored soldiers pouring out of the city, their march aimed straight toward the Mangrove Forest.

“This time, I won’t let you escape again!” Blei snarled, clad in red-and-black armor while mounted upon a towering, ferocious beast. The beast let out a savage roar and charged at full speed, with the black-armored soldiers swiftly following in formation.

Players outside the city, eager for a spectacle, quickly trailed after them, setting up livestreams, commentary, and all-in-one coverage.

Meanwhile, the busy Yae-hime received a message from Nangong Lin. The latter praised her a few times before moving on to serious business.

As expected, the Direct Army’s troops were on their way. Through the attached video, Yae-hime caught sight of Blei. “So that guy’s actually making a move himself. That’s a bit troublesome.”

Looking at the scattered equipment around her, Yae-hime sighed with a trace of regret. There was simply no way to pick it all up in the time left. Some of it would have to be abandoned.

“Rare gear is worth the most, make sure to grab as much of that as possible. As for Common and Uncommon gear, whatever’s left behind can count as charity.”

From Nangong Lin’s video, she could see a swarm of players rushing toward her direction like a bustling marketplace. Closing her game interface, she quickly began sweeping up the loot, striving to maximize her gains within the limited time.

---

Outside the game, in Dorado, USA, at a branch of the Central Intelligence Agency.

Mira had already logged out, staring at her phone with a grave expression. On the screen was an encrypted message sent from the Department of Homeland Security.

“That one’s danger rating just got bumped up to S-rank in one go.” Naturally, the _one_ she referred to was Yae-hime. “This isn’t good. If my colleagues at Homeland Security kill her first, then who am I supposed to take revenge on?”

Mira tossed her phone aside, leaning back against the soft sofa cushions, tilting her head to gaze at the blank white ceiling above. “No, it’s already a stretch whether or not she can survive tonight. How frustrating.”

Thinking of how likely it was that the Black-hearted Princess would end up slain by Lucky, she let out a soft sigh. “Ah, in the end, she’s still too young. Offending someone who must never be offended can only be repaid with death.”

Yet despite her words, Mira herself was only eighteen years old. In terms of mental age, Yae-hime was actually older than her.

---

Cathay, Huadu City, Zhang family estate.

Taurus lay sprawled on the floor, gasping for breath in ragged gulps. The room around him was a complete mess, as if it had been ransacked. In fact, this wreckage was the result of Taurus’ own violent rampage.

Now that his fit of rage had passed, all that remained was fear. Fear of the Black-hearted Princess. Fear of death.

“Uuuu…” Hugging his arms tightly, Taurus trembled uncontrollably. His pale face was ghostly, and his eyes flickered with panic. In his mind, the scene of his death replayed over and over, every second crystal clear.

He had been so close. Just one step away from success. But that single step had become an unbridgeable chasm that ultimately led to his doom. The world collapsed, and it all ended in tragedy. Why had it turned out like this?

He thought and thought, and at last, came to a conclusion. “S.K.Y.! It’s all his fault! If only he had given the order for a full assault right away! Yes! It was all his fault! He made me suffer this humiliating defeat! That damned mutt! I swear I won’t let you off!”

Venomous words spilled from Taurus’ mouth, echoing repeatedly through the trashed room.

Meanwhile, S.K.Y. sat with his back against a damp stone wall, staring silently at the flickering candlelight ahead, his expression weary and somber. This was his hideout, nestled halfway up a mountain in Qingcheng, Linhnan.

His grandfather had once lived here and had built a simple mud-brick hut. Now it had fallen into decay. But beneath the house lay a secret, a hidden path that led deep into a cavern filled with stalactites.

As long as he brought enough food, he could hide in this place for a year or more without issue.

“That useless fool, Taurus.” He suddenly spoke aloud. “All talk, and still managed to screw everything up! We were this close. If he had just acted a few seconds faster, we could’ve won! Trash. Idiot. Worthless!”

With every word, his fury built. His pitch-black eyes began to flush red, like pools of blood. “Curse you, Taurus. Curse you, Black-hearted Princess. I won’t let either of you get away with this!”

As he roared, S.K.Y. dug his nails into his arm, tearing open his skin and drawing blood. The dim candlelight stretched his silhouette along the stone walls, making him appear taller. Suddenly, the shadow behind him opened blood-red eyes. And a gaping maw full of crimson teeth. It moved its mouth, as if speaking, but no sound came forth.

---

In-game. Blei barreled forward atop his ferocious beast, finally arriving at the scene ten minutes later. But it was too late. There wasn’t a soul in sight. The Black-hearted Princess had clearly vanished long ago.

As for the players who had died here, none had yet dared to resurrect. Their fear of the Black-hearted Princess had reached an entirely new level. Until they were certain she had left the area, none of them would dare log back in.

“She ran fast!” Blei clenched his iron fist, frustration dripping from his voice. Though he had sensed they might come up empty-handed, having his hunch confirmed still left him furious.

“All units spread out! Search the entire area! Report anything suspicious immediately!” He stared ahead and issued the command with a sweeping gesture. His troops responded instantly, fanning out to begin a meticulous search.

The nearby players, who had followed hoping for drama, felt disappointed. They had expected a showdown. But their disappointment quickly turned into elation. Scattered on the battlefield were a few pieces of equipment lying untouched!

In an instant, excited players surged forward, pouncing like rabid dogs to snatch whatever visible loot they could find.

Elsewhere, Yae-hime reclined comfortably in a luxurious beast-drawn carriage, gazing up at the endless blue sky, the corners of her lips curling into a smile. She murmured softly to herself, “Reaping leeks… really is addictive.”

+++

# 709 – Aftermath and the Eve Before the Duel

Overseas. The Okinawa Islands.

At this time, the Grandmasters and S-rank transcendents in the Ota Dojo had already finished a midday meal. It was not particularly lavish, but it was refined and well-prepared.

With their bellies full of food and drink, a touch of drowsiness naturally crept in. However, none of those present went to take a nap. Instead, they sat together in a circle, chatting and boasting, showing no trace of tension.

In truth, there was no need for them to feel tense. After all, the only one who would be stepping into the arena tonight was Lucky. Since the star of the evening himself showed no sign of nervousness, why should the others feel on edge? They were merely here to watch a performance. There was no need to act as if they were part of the play.

“Grandmaster Hong, we’ll be counting on your performance tonight,” said the S-rank transcendent from Britain, known as the God of Thunder, with a smile.

“Haha, no problem. I guarantee I won’t let you down.” Lucky cupped his hands toward him.

This man, about fifty years old, with a full head of golden hair and the title of Thunder God, was named John. In Britain, there were likely so many men named John that a falling billboard could kill a dozen of them. It was an utterly common, almost cliché, name, comparable to a “Xiao Ming[1](https://re-library.com/translations/reborn-as-a-transcendent/volume-3/chapter-709-aftermath-and-the-eve-before-the-duel/#easy-footnote-bottom-1-113115)” in Cathay.

John had a bit of personal history with Yae-hime. Some time ago, the one known as Lightning Wolf, who had charged into Cathay only to be blasted to death by Mylene, had once been mentored and assisted by John in developing his electric-type abilities. Strictly speaking, Lightning Wolf could be considered half a disciple of Thunder God.

Of course, John didn’t believe for a second that it was Yae-hime who had killed him. Still, the fact remained that David had gone to Cathay because of her. In the end, he died. That debt, at least in part, had to be counted against Yae-hime.

To put it bluntly, John was here more for the show than for revenge. As for avenging a disciple? That was out of the question. John wasn’t foolish enough to make enemies of Cathay’s top powers over a half-baked disciple.

“Grandmaster Hong, may your flag rise in victory,” said Wind Lord Kim Tae-gi, a Grandmaster from Korea, with a calm expression.

Unlike John, he had a real grudge against Yae-hime. His disciples, Jin Junmin and Desmond, had both died miserably at her hands. That damned Princess clearly had Grandmaster-level strength, yet pretended to be weak and lured his beloved disciples to their brutal deaths.

This grudge was one of life and death, utterly irreconcilable. Unfortunately, someone else had gotten ahead of him in seeking vengeance. Now all he could do was take some comfort in watching her die miserably.

“Definitely, without a doubt!” Lucky cupped his hands in return.

At the table, the guests chatted and laughed, the atmosphere growing lively. This group of powerhouses was rather friendly with Lucky and Grandmaster Ota.

Another group of experts was currently resting in their hotel rooms, waiting for nightfall. As for the outcome of the duel, they already had a clear prediction in mind. It would be an overwhelming victory for Lucky.

Most of them were simply here to enjoy the show, while also taking the chance to gauge the true extent of his strength. The weaker ones were mainly sent by their masters to watch and show some courtesy to Lucky. As for the result? It didn’t really matter to them.

---

In-game.

After some travel, Yae-hime finally made her way back to Aoma Village. By now, Angelica had already gotten somewhat familiar with the Fiat siblings. They were getting along quite decently.

Upon seeing Yae-hime return, everyone’s faces lit up with joy as they called out in unison: “Princess!”

“I’m back. Are you two getting used to things here?” Yae-hime looked at the Fiat siblings.  

“Mm! It’s so much better here than in the city. We feel free,” Aurora said with a smile.  

“Yes.” Fiat nodded in agreement.

Compared to the commoners district, the atmosphere here was clearly much more pleasant. What they didn’t know was that Aoma Village hadn’t always been like this.

“As long as you’re happy. We’ll be staying here for a while.” Yae-hime said with a gentle tone.  

“I’ll take good care of them,” Angelica replied with a calm smile.  

“Mm, I’ll leave it to you then.” Yae-hime nodded, then seemed to remember something. “Oh right, Angelica, can you arrange a beast carriage to head to Aureole Town and pick someone up for me?”

Based on her estimate, the epidemic over there should have already been handled by Micha. Rather than leaving Layna alone in the town, it would be better to bring her over so they could all look out for one another.

Besides, she would soon be producing Holy Water here. Constantly traveling back and forth would be a huge waste of time.

‘It’s just more convenient to base operations out of Aoma Village.’

More importantly, she wasn’t sure how far Alicia’s preparations had come. If she kept running around, Lili might not be able to find her.

“No problem, I’ll make the arrangements right away… Princess, could you give me that person’s full details?” Angelica had taken a few steps but then stopped and turned back to Yae-hime with the question.

Yae-hime wrote down the details on a piece of paper, then took out a vial of antidote from her ring and handed both to Angelica. “Just have someone deliver this potion to her,” Yae-hime said.

Taking the note and the potion, Angelica glanced at the information written on the paper. After a brief hesitation, she spoke up. “Princess, I think I should go myself.”

“Why?” Yae-hime asked.  

“This Layna is a girl, isn’t she? Sending a strange man to pick her up just doesn’t feel right.” Angelica explained calmly.

Hearing that, Yae-hime paused in thought. She had to admit Angelica had a point. She’d overlooked that. “Mm, sorry to trouble you.” She gently patted Angelica on the shoulder.

“It’s nothing. I’ll be back soon,” Angelica replied with a cheerful smile, gave a slight bow, and swiftly headed out.

Yae-hime sat down with the Fiat siblings for tea and conversation. It was a leisurely, pleasant time. While things were calm and relaxing on this end, over at the Mangrove Forest, it was utter chaos.

“This one’s mine!” a warrior player bellowed.  

“It’s mine!” a holy knight across from him shouted in return.

The two had both grabbed hold of a piece of Uncommon armor and were now locked in a tug-of-war over it. Scenes like this played out again and again in the ruined outskirts of the Mangrove Forest.

By now, the early players had already swept the ground clean of loot. Those who arrived later could only dig through cracks in the earth, scavenging whatever was left. As time went on, even the players who had been killed began to revive, and they, too, joined the treasure hunt.

Compared to the others, these revived players were even more eager and desperate. After all, it was their gear that had been dropped. If they managed to reclaim any of it, they wouldn’t consider the loss too great.

Some aggressive players even resorted to outright robbery, sparking fierce fights. For a time, the situation spiraled out of control.

Still, no matter how chaotic things became, it was an outsider problem. The locals simply couldn’t be bothered. Seeing that the search had come up empty, Blei immediately led his team back to the city. He could already guarantee he’d be getting a good scolding from the emperor the moment he returned.

Along the way, sighs of frustration and regret echoed nonstop.

---

Before the sun had even set, Angelica had already brought Layna back to Aoma Village.

The group chatted for a while, and when Yae-hime noticed the time was getting late, she excused herself and left the living room under the pretense of having something to do. She returned to the guest room and logged off.

In truth, she really did have something to take care of.

---

Outside the game, within the City of Chaos.

Yae-hime slowly opened her eyes, rose from bed, and exhaled softly. “Two more hours… time to get ready.” Even though the outcome of her duel with Lucky was practically set in stone, since this was her first official duel, Yae-hime still wanted to make her appearance in the best form possible.

“What kind of outfit should I wear?”

Yes—her so-called preparation was entirely about her clothes.

+++

# 710 – I Would Never Wear Something Like That~

Standing in front of the wardrobe, Yae-hime wore a rare serious expression.

“Formal dress… looks nice, sure, but I’m going to a duel, not a banquet. Normal skirts… with that many spectators watching, if I accidentally raise my leg too high, wouldn’t that be a huge loss? No way, that’s out of the question! Professional outfit might work, but… isn’t the skirt a bit too short? Bunny girl costume… Wait a minute, why do I even have such a weird outfit!?”

“That’s something I brought back on a whim,” a cute voice suddenly rang out in the room.

“Little Blue, why did you put this weird costume in my wardrobe?” Yae-hime turned her head and looked unamused at Little Blue, who had just teleported into the room.

“I thought it would suit you, Master, so I brought it back. I even paid for it properly!” Little Blue replied with a playful grin.

“That’s not the point. It’s not about whether you paid for it or not. I would never wear something like this, so why’d you even buy it?” Yae-hime tossed the bunny girl outfit out of the wardrobe.

“Master, that outfit cost 55,000, you know,” Little Blue said with a hint of regret.

Upon hearing that, Yae-hime spun around and leapt forward, catching the outfit firmly before it hit the ground. “You spent 55,000 on a few scraps of cloth?” Her heart ached.

What a colossal waste. With that much money, the little ones at home could’ve eaten for several days…

‘Wait, only several days? What kind of bottomless pits am I feeding!?’

Some things are fine when ignored, but shocking when calculated. Having grown used to spending extravagantly lately, Yae-hime hadn’t really paid attention to her household expenses. But now that her wallet was nearly empty, her sensitivity to money had suddenly heightened.

For Yae-hime, a ¥55,000 outfit was an absolute luxury. What she didn’t know was that the outfits Nangong Lin had custom-ordered for her all cost far more than that.

“I just wanted to see you wear it,” Little Blue said in a cutesy voice.

“Next time, you’re absolutely not allowed to bring back weird stuff without my permission.” Yae-hime shot her a glare, then reluctantly placed the bunny girl outfit back into the wardrobe.

“Wait a second… this tennis outfit, this nurse outfit, this leather suit, and this swimsuit…did you sneak these in too?” Looking at the new additions inside the wardrobe, Yae-hime’s eyelid twitched involuntarily.

“Mhm! I know Master’s measurements perfectly. They’ll fit like a glove!” Little Blue boasted with pride. And promptly received a flick to the forehead.

“Oww!”

“If you buy clothes without permission again, it’ll be fifty flicks next time!” Yae-hime warned.

This time, she didn’t even ask how much they cost, she didn’t want her heart broken. Thankfully, barring any accidents, she was likely to come into a windfall tonight. That would at least temporarily ease her financial woes.

‘Sigh… Who knows when my poor little city will finally be fully repaired.’

All the money she’d earned recently, minus daily expenses, had been funneled into Chaos City’s restoration, and yet only a tiny portion had been repaired.

‘The days of poverty… still seem far from over.’

After rummaging through the wardrobe, Yae-hime ultimately chose a tracksuit. It was a reluctant choice. Because every other outfit either had skirts or was completely inappropriate for going outside.

“I kinda missed this.” Donning a black-and-white tracksuit, the kind commonly seen in Roc City, Yae-hime couldn’t help but recall her early days after the transformation. It hadn’t been long ago, yet it felt like it had been ages.[1](https://re-library.com/translations/reborn-as-a-transcendent/volume-3/chapter-710-i-would-never-wear-something-like-that/#easy-footnote-bottom-1-113119) That feeling of nostalgia, was itself nothing more than an illusion.

“The time for me to change back should be near,” she murmured while gazing at the now-closed wardrobe. The premise for changing back was that she’d gain access to the Saint Demon Roulette. Since the item came from there, the method to undo it could only be found there as well.

“Change back? Change what back?” Little Blue asked in confusion.  

“It’s nothing.” Yae-hime shook her head. “You haven’t had dinner yet, have you?”  

“Nope! We were waiting for you, Master!” Little Blue nodded quickly.  

“Let’s go together then. There’s still over an hour before the duel starts.”

Yae-hime patted her head, then stepped out of the room and headed toward the dining hall. As for tonight’s battle, she shared the same view as those Grandmasters. It was bound to be a one-sided match, nothing more than a formality.

There was no need to worry about underhanded tactics either. Whether that was due to Lucky’s blind confidence or lack of ability was still uncertain. All in all, this was a perfectly fair duel.

While Yae-hime was having dinner with the adorable ones at home… In an affluent neighborhood in San Francisco, United States—

“Looks like we’re going to lose at least a few hundred million tonight.” In a lavishly decorated, spacious living room, a middle-aged blond man leaned back against a luxury sofa, a cigar resting between his lips. He spoke with an indifferent tone, as if the figure meant nothing to him.

“Only a few hundred million? That’s barely worth any attention at all,” remarked the elderly man seated across from him. He wore a finely tailored robe, his face withered, his voice calm.

“That’s actually quite a bit, Father,” the middle-aged man replied, shaking his head. His name was Carlsberg Rivest, current head of the Rivest Conglomerate in the United States. He was also one of the country’s closed beta players, and Leon’s uncle.

Sitting across from him was the previous head of the family, Budweiser Rivest.

“Oh? Did something unexpected happen?” Budweiser raised an eyebrow, intrigued.

“Yes. That Princess apparently has quite a few supporters in Cathay. We’ve already received nearly 60 million US dollars in wagers on her.” Carlsberg explained.

“Heh. Must be a bunch of rich fools,” Budweiser chuckled.

They hadn’t set up this betting event with the primary goal of turning a profit. That didn’t mean they would turn down the chance to make money from it. Their family understood very well what high society truly craved— thrill. A thrill that transcended everything else!

Most pleasures that ordinary people enjoyed had long ceased to stir the senses of the elite. Things obtained too easily simply failed to excite.

“When I was young, I often wondered why ancient civilizations had things like gladiator arenas. It wasn’t until I came of age that I finally understood. It was about the thrill. That soul-shaking, spirit-rending thrill is what we should be chasing,” Budweiser said slowly.

As he spoke, a twisted smile crept across his withered face. It was under his leadership that their family had risen to its current status. “War, battle, bloodshed, the clash of weapons, the cries of pain, the shadow of death… the shock and excitement they bring are what we’ve always sold.”

Carlsberg chuckled. Their family was unlike typical conglomerates, tainted with the stench of blood. “While the outcome is all but certain, tonight’s Grandmaster Duel still has its highlights.”

Carlsberg set his cigar down. “I imagine elites from all over the world will be watching.”

“Watching from behind a screen… what cowards,” Budweiser sneered in disdain. If not for his old bones being too fragile to travel, he would’ve definitely gone to watch it in person.

A Grandmaster-level duel, such a thing was rare and precious. That was true, transcendental combat, beyond the limits of human strength.

“Heh, you can’t really say that…” Carlsberg began, but before he could finish, his phone suddenly rang. He pulled it out and checked the screen, and his pupils involuntarily contracted.

+++

# 711 – Bad Omens Always Come True

“What is it?” Budweiser asked when he noticed the change in his son’s expression.

“My father, you may not believe it, but just now, someone placed two hundred million on Princess.” Carlsberg gave a bitter smile.

“Who has money to throw around like that?” Two hundred million US dollars was not a huge sum to Budweiser. Yet the act of tossing that much money into the saltwater sea still piqued his curiosity.

“The Mo Family of Cathay,” Carlsberg said.  

“That superfamily? Interesting.” Budweiser chuckled.  

“It seems the rumors of the Mo Family secretly protecting Princess were not groundless.” Carlsberg put away his phone and spoke in his usual flat tone. His surprise had come not from the amount of the wager but from the chosen target.  

“Two hundred million, most likely just a gesture of support.” Budweiser’s lips curled into a mocking smile. “Too bad, tonight that Princess will be beaten to death before everyone’s eyes.”

Ironic, truly ironic!

“It doesn’t seem that simple,” Carlsberg muttered with a furrowed brow. “My father, do you think that Princess has any chance of winning?”  

“None. Not even the slightest,” Budweiser declared. He had studied martial artists extensively and naturally understood the gulf between them.

Although Lucky and Princess were both Grandmasters, the former had already stepped into the Intermediate Phase, while the latter had only just entered the Primary Phase. The gap between Primary and Intermediate might appear small, yet in truth it was like heaven and earth. Countless Primary Grandmasters had spent their entire lives unable to cross into Intermediate.

“The Mo Family throwing away two hundred million like this is certainly thought-provoking,” Carlsberg remarked.  

“They’re only making a gesture. Nothing worth caring about,” Budweiser replied with complete indifference.  

“Yes.” Carlsberg nodded, though unease lingered in his heart. Still, since his father had spoken so firmly, it had to be correct.

At the same time. On Baiding Island. The lights blazed so brightly it was as though day had descended. Several dozen kilometers from the square, massive generators roared without pause, supplying an endless current of power to the site.

At the docks, several luxury yachts were moored alongside an ostentatious fisheries patrol vessel. Had the ship still been fitted with vertical missile launchers, it would have been truly frightening. But unfortunately, it was now nothing more than a genuine fisheries patrol ship.

In the dueling square, several hundred people had already gathered, most of them martial artists and transcendents. A smaller portion consisted of prominent figures from across the world.

Lucky sat in a redwood chair, sipping black tea brewed by his subordinates, utterly at ease as though on vacation. There was not the slightest trace of tension in him; in fact, he seemed faintly delighted. The thought that in less than an hour he would crush that detestable Princess beneath his palm only made his mood better and better.

No one spoke on the scene. It was not that they didn’t want to speak, but the pressure exuded by the masters present was overwhelming. If those experts chose silence, the weaker ones naturally dared not utter a word. For all they knew, they might offend some short-tempered powerhouse and be beaten half to death on the spot. And if that happened, they would have no choice but to accept their fate.

After all, these monsters that had surpassed human limits rarely acted with reason.

**Tap, tap, tap!**

Suddenly, the sound of footsteps echoed. Two graceful figures appeared not far away. One was tall and slender, with delicate features and waist-length hair, dressed in a flowing black gown. The other was petite and adorable, clad in a sky-blue dress, looking no older than an elementary schooler in her fifth or sixth year.

The moment the two entered the square, they immediately drew attention. As late arrivals, being noticed was inevitable. Yet such a pair—one tall, one small—naturally sparked curiosity. In an occasion like this, was it really appropriate to bring along a child? Some couldn’t help but wonder in their hearts.

Among the gathered elites, some recognized Pixie at once, and any sense of surprise quickly faded. As for the young girl at her side who looked only around twelve, they couldn’t even be bothered to pay attention. If only they knew that this little girl was actually the strongest among everyone present, jaws and eyes alike would surely have dropped to the ground.

“No one seems intent on stirring trouble,” Mylene whispered softly. She had only debuted a year ago, and most of her missions were top secret. Even in the capital, few knew her true background, let alone these foreign powerhouses.

“This island will be without dispute in just a few months. What neighboring country would dare stir up trouble now?” Pixie smiled as she spoke.

“True.” Mylene nodded lightly.

On the other side, Lucky set down his teacup and glanced over, his gaze carrying a hint of surprise. But it vanished just as quickly. After all, the place was teeming with experts. Even with Pixie present, she could not hope to stir up much of a storm.

The two casually found a spot to stand, saying nothing, simply waiting in silence.

The square was shrouded in a heavy air of quiet.

Under the same sky, within the City of Chaos.

“Thirty minutes left. More than enough time.” Yae-hime had already finished dinner. Now she changed into a black-and-white tracksuit, slipped on a pair of white Anta sneakers, and slung an Adidas sports bag over her right shoulder.

She looked less like someone going to a duel and more like someone heading out for a night jog.

“Hopefully things won’t go too far off track,” she murmured anxiously as she glanced at her sports bag. Inside was a change of clothes. If she was unlucky and got teleported into water, ending up drenched, at least she would have something dry to wear.

Little Blue had thoughtfully packed the clothes in vacuum-sealed bags. Even if submerged for over ten minutes, they would remain dry.

“Master, are you ready?” Little Blue suddenly asked.  

“All set. I’ll be back soon. You all take good care of the house.” Yae-hime replied.  

“Mhm!” the Vera clones nodded in unison.  

“Master, safe travels!” At that moment, Little Blue’s eyes glowed with a blue light.

“Safe travels…?” Yae-hime suddenly thought of the ominous phrase ‘lost during teleportation’, and an uneasy chill crept into her heart. She wanted to say something, but before the words could leave her lips, her figure dissolved into a burst of white light and vanished.

The space trembled faintly.

“Hm?” Little Blue tilted her head, her face full of puzzlement. “This teleportation feels a little different from usual. Never mind. The deviation shouldn’t be too big.”

With that, she floated off toward the kitchen and instructed Chef One to prepare tonight’s late-night snack.

---

Somewhere within the space near Baiding Island.

‘What’s going on… This teleportation feels completely different from usual!’

At that moment, Yae-hime found herself suspended in a strange place filled with radiant colors and overflowing with spatial energy. It was something she had never encountered before.

‘Teleportation failure?’ The thought alone made her scalp tingle, a chill seeping through her entire body. ‘I can’t possibly be that unlucky!’

She tried to move her hand, only to realize she couldn’t even twitch a single finger. It was as if she had completely merged into this wondrous realm, becoming part of the space itself. The sensation was utterly surreal.

‘This is bad… I have a terrible feeling about this…’ As though to confirm her premonition, the colorful space suddenly collapsed. Multicolored shards scattered like shattering glass.

In the next instant, she saw only endless darkness. From within that pitch-black void, a faint yet all-too-familiar aura emanated. An aura that was terrifyingly dangerous!

+++

# 712 – The Main Lead? I Gave Up That Role Long Ago

Although nothing could be seen, Yae-hime sensed something racing toward her at high speed. And it carried with it an aura of extreme danger. This aura was one she knew all too well.

Without question, it was the predecessor of that mutated energy within Allie— a spatial storm! Though called a storm, in truth it was an invisible fluctuation of energy that usually appeared within unstable fractured spaces.

Clearly, Yae-hime was now within such a fractured boundary between spaces. That was why she had encountered this terrifying phenomenon.

‘This doesn’t make sense. I shouldn’t be this unlucky!’ Yae-hime racked her brain but could not understand why she had run into such a near-impossible danger.

At this moment, thinking too much was useless. In this strange space where time itself seemed to stand still, all she could do was sit and wait for death. She had no idea how much time had passed.

Yae-hime only felt something flow straight through her body. Then, part of it remained inside her, raging wildly! This was nothing like the weakened, mutated remnants of a spatial storm that had lingered in Allie’s body. The destructive power was worlds apart.

In just an instant, Yae-hime felt as though she had died hundreds of times over. That agony was more than ten times worse than being cut apart by a thousand blades. It was as if both her body and soul were being sliced into pieces, tossed into a boiling hotpot, and then chewed apart bit by bit.

The torment made her wish for death on the spot. Had it been anyone else, they might have gone mad within seconds. Yet Yae-hime was someone who had truly died once before. Her mental fortitude far surpassed that of ordinary people.

By gritting her teeth and enduring a while longer, she finally felt the situation begin to improve. If this world had a system, it would surely be ringing nonstop right now, announcing the insane surge of her Spatial Attribute.

It felt like only a few seconds had passed, and yet it also felt like several years. The pain in Yae-hime’s body had vanished, replaced instead with the illusion that space itself was hers to command.

She tried moving her hand. To her surprise, it actually worked. Before this, no matter how hard she had tried, not even a single finger could budge.

‘Blessing in disguise? I doubt it’s that simple…’

Even though she had gained considerable benefits, Yae-hime did not feel the slightest bit happy. She couldn’t shake the sense that something about this was off.

Logically, as the artifact spirit of the City of Chaos, Little Blue might make mistakes, but never anything this absurd. For such a minuscule probability event to land squarely on her, it felt wrong no matter how she thought about it.

And in the end, she had even come out of it with benefits. Even with her Luck stat at 666, she still found the coincidence far too outrageous.

‘There’s a different aura lingering in this space!’

All of a sudden, Yae-hime’s eyes sharpened as she looked upward. Above her was nothing but endless darkness, where nothing could be seen. At this moment, she was no longer relying on her eyes to perceive.

As Yae-hime’s perception of space improved, the way she _saw_ this pitch-black realm had completely changed.

Threads. She could see countless threads. And among them, a faint trace of lingering energy. It was not left behind by the spatial storm, but by someone, or perhaps some being.

‘It was this thing that interfered with my teleportation!’ The instant she discovered that trace of energy, Yae-hime immediately came to a realization. Her predicament had indeed been deliberately orchestrated by someone! ‘Just who, and why would they do this?’

---

At the same time. Within what seemed like an infinitely vast white space, a soft laugh suddenly echoed.

At the center of the space— no, rather, no matter where she stood, it would be the center— sat a girl dressed in a flowing white gown. Her skin was as pale as snow, her long legs crossed elegantly as she reclined upon a throne of nothingness, exuding an aura of nobility.

But it was not a matter of temperament. She herself was the highest and most exalted existence, standing above all living beings.

“So, I’ve been discovered.” Her words carried an oppressive weight, yet at the same time carried a playful lilt, oddly making her feel approachable. Her face must have been indescribably beautiful, but regretfully, some mysterious power veiled it, preventing anyone from seeing it clearly.

“You must hurry and grow stronger, my…” Her voice gradually softened, then cut off completely. No one knew what she had intended to say.

Elsewhere, Yae-hime withdrew her gaze and slowly raised her right hand. When it came to that mysterious existence, she had given up on pursuing answers. She had no choice but to give up. The other party’s strength was far too unfathomable. No matter how she searched, she would never uncover anything meaningful.

‘That trace of energy… it must have been intentionally left behind by them. I can’t tell if I should feel relieved or uneasy.’

Letting out a quiet sigh in her heart, Yae-hime chose to stop thinking about it. No matter how she turned it over in her mind, she would never figure it out. It was far more practical to focus on escaping this space.

Just then, a sharp crack echoed through the void. Unlike the earlier silent shattering, this time it came with sound.

Yae-hime’s scalp prickled, and a chill swept through her heart. She could sense a terrifying force rushing toward her at incredible speed. Though it was weaker than a spatial storm, it still carried immense threat!

In an instant, Yae-hime focused all her power on defense. The next moment, that dreadful force crashed into her with the violence of Type-59 Star Destroyers[1](https://re-library.com/translations/reborn-as-a-transcendent/volume-3/chapter-712-the-main-lead-i-gave-up-that-role-long-ago/#easy-footnote-bottom-1-113129) breaking the sound barrier!

At the same time, a section of space near Baiding Island suddenly split apart, forming a dreadful fissure. The next instant, a black shadow shot out from within, plunging into the sea like a deep-water bomb and blasting up a towering pillar of water.

Though the commotion here was immense, it did not affect the plaza nearby. After all, Baiding Island was vast.

At this moment, only fifteen minutes remained before seven o’clock. The atmosphere at the plaza was very different from before. It had grown restless. Within the crowd, whispers rose and fell.

“It’s almost seven and she still hasn’t come. What kind of diva does she think she is?” an S-rank transcendent said with displeasure.

Although the agreed time had not yet arrived, with everyone else already gathered, the absence of the other key figure inevitably stirred irritation.

“Perhaps she’s too scared to show up,” someone chuckled softly.  

“In such an important duel, if she doesn’t appear, Cathay will lose all face.”  

“Exactly.”  

“Hah, no wonder she wouldn’t dare come. Intermediate versus Primary, that’s an overwhelming difference.”  

“The outcome will be decided within thirty moves,” declared a Grandmaster from Korea.  

“Someone’s merely late, and yet you gossip like this. Honestly…” Grandmaster Ota shook his head.

Hearing that, the other powerhouses flushed slightly and fell obediently silent.

Checking the time, there were thirteen minutes left.

“Looks like she’s not coming.” A spectator standing at the highest point of the plaza swept his military-grade binoculars across the surroundings. The sea lay calm and still. Not a ripple, not even the shadow of a fish, let alone a boat.

“To lose without a fight, how laughable.”  

“And here I was, actually looking forward to this.”  

“What a waste of my time!”  

“What a spineless coward!”

The murmurs within the crowd grew louder and more irritating by the minute. Naturally, Mylene and Pixie knew that Yae-hime was not someone who would back down at the last moment.

“Big Sis must’ve run into some trouble,” Mylene whispered under her breath.  

“Mhm, most likely.” Pixie nodded, worry spreading across her face.

**Tap, tap, tap!**

At that moment, Lucky rose from his redwood chair and strode toward the center of the square. His expression was calm, his demeanor relaxed. To him, it made no difference whether Yae-hime came or not.

‘If you don’t come, you’ll regret it for the rest of your life.’

Dressed in a bright yellow kung fu uniform, Lucky clasped his hands behind his back and stood tall, a faint smile playing on his lips.

Time trickled by, and soon it was 6:58 PM. By now, both the audience at the square and those watching the livestream had grown thoroughly impatient.

“Damn it, she really isn’t coming!”  

“This is nothing but a murder of my time!”  

“So this is Cathay’s so-called Grandmaster?”  

“To think she would retreat at the last moment, what a disappointment!”  

“Hah, gutless scum.”  

“From now on, all martial artists of Cathay should be treated like sick cats.”  

“F̲u̲c̲k̲, is she coming or not?!”  

“S̲h̲i̲t̲!”

The words filling the square grew fouler and fouler. Mylene and Pixie wanted to cover their ears. No, more than that, they wanted to beat this rabble into silence. The appointed time hadn’t even arrived yet! But more than silencing the crowd, they worried for Yae-hime’s safety.

Time continued to slip away. At last, only two minutes remained. Then finally, only five seconds. Lucky glanced at the time, his expression turning solemn. “It seems she has lost her nerve. To have wasted everyone’s precious time, I sincerely apologize.”

Just as his words fell, the clock struck exactly seven.

“Who’s the dog that said I lost my nerve?” Right as people were about to erupt in collective frustration, a clear, beautiful voice suddenly rang out.

Everyone turned toward the sound, but saw no one. Confusion rippled through the crowd. How could there be a voice, yet no figure?

“There!”

Someone with keen hearing and eyesight finally caught the source a second later. She was in midair!

“Big Sis!”  

“Princess!”

No… someone else had noticed even earlier. Mylene and Pixie had already turned their gazes skyward the very moment the voice was heard, and saw Yae-hime hovering in the air.

A few moments later, the rest of the crowd followed their gaze, and then the entire square fell deathly silent. Apart from Mylene and Pixie, everyone was so shocked they were struck speechless.

Because Princess was walking through the sky! The astonishment of ordinary people was nothing compared to that of the Grandmasters.

“Walking upon the void… that’s the Martial Saint Realm!” Grandmaster Ota cried out involuntarily.  

“This… how is this possible?!”  

“It must be a trick, right?”  

“This is impossible!” Lucky’s calm composure shattered, his face twisting as he spoke.

An eighteen-year-old girl little brat, and she was a Martial Saint? How could he possibly believe that? It had to be an act! She had purposely arrived late, just to buy time for this trick.

Her intent was obvious— to shake his confidence!

“A petty illusion. Don’t think you can fool me!” Lucky roared.

His voice thundered like spring lightning, jolting the crowd out of their stupor. When the transcendents present thought carefully, they too found it absurd.

High above, Yae-hime ignored them all and continued her steady walk through the air. She was clad in a simple, elegant ancient gown, her silken ribbons fluttering in the wind. She looked like a fairy descending from the Ninth Heaven, breathtaking beyond words.

The moon slipped out from behind the dark clouds, scattering silver light that draped her in a luminous cloak, adding an air of divinity to her beauty.

As that ethereal figure slowly descended, the square grew unnaturally silent. Every pair of eyes locked onto her, as though bewitched. Their souls trembled under the weight of the sight.

++++

# Two as One Princesses - Chapter 165 - Lunch, 5th Floor Resident, and Magic Eyes

I was having a hard time deciding on lunch, but then I saw they had egg sandwiches, so I went with that. To be precise, it was part of a set of three sandwiches.  

Though I call it a sandwich, it wasn’t the typical kind made with sliced bread. Instead, the fillings were tucked between English muffin-like buns.

Price-wise, it’s a bit pricier than the average. Comparing this to the food outside of the academy, it’s like a slightly expensive lunch. Unlike yesterday, since it’s in the middle of lunchtime, there are a lot of people, and it’s hard to find a seat.  

I used a full power detection to find unoccupied seats and marched straight ahead.

『That’s a luxurious way of using magic.』  

『I see it more as a convenient way of using magic.』  

『Fair point. Would I be able to do the same in the future?』  

『If you solely focus on practicing detection, you could probably even do it immediately, I think?』

Ciel uses detection to maneuver herself advantageously during battles, while I generally use it for enemy detection. Because of that, Ciel doesn’t really need to increase her detection range. And perhaps recognizing that as well, she doesn’t put as much effort into expanding it as I do.  

This is why I answered the way I did, to which Ciel responded with a giggle, 『It’s better to leave it to Ain.』

『By the way, Ain, do you like sandwiches?』  

『I don’t particularly hate them; I just felt like eating some right now. I’m craving eggs.』  

『Eggs are delicious, after all.』  

『In my old world, we even ate eggs raw.』  

『Eggs can be eaten raw?』  

『It’s best not to do that. You’ll likely upset your stomach.』

Even in my old world, people are advised against eating raw eggs outside of Japan. I recall that it’s only edible in Japan because of rigorous quality control.  

Generally, it’s considered crazy to eat eggs raw. The consensus is more like, _It’s amazing these guys eat eggs raw!_ or something along those lines.  

I don’t really want to eat raw eggs now either.

『And you ate it like that, Ain?』  

『Because it was fine to do where I live. There were people who would even detoxify poisonous food or find under which condition deadly food could be eaten safely, you see.』  

『Now I’m getting curious. I’d love to visit there at least once.』

It’s not limited to Japan: if you go around the world, you’d probably see many delicious and weird foods.  

I don’t plan on recreating my old world’s food here. My cooking was basically just slapping random things together since I live alone, so I don’t think I can recreate it anyway.

There are four open seats in total. All four of them are positioned by the aisle, so we got an aisle seat.  

Naturally, the individual following us necessarily has to sit on one of them. But I have no idea why she’s sitting right in front of me.  

Well, she’s basically a stranger, so I’ll ignore her. I’ll only respond if she initiates.

『The food here really is delicious.』  

『It’s tasty for its price, isn’t it? They’re simple but seem to be made with care.』  

『Also, it’s interesting how they flavor their food slightly differently compared to Central.』  

『That’s true. It’s small things like these that display a country’s unique character.』

Personally, I prefer Central’s flavors, but this is delicious in its own way.  

How do I describe it? Central’s flavors are deep, while the flavors here are dense. It’s hard to explain.

『By the way, what’s going on with the girl in front of us? She seems focused on eating, but she hasn’t eaten much of her food.』

Just as she said, the mysterious girl is looking at her plate intently while taking small bites of her food. Unlike Palra, she’s like a small animal.

『This is just a wild guess, but perhaps she simply isn’t familiar with how the cafeteria works?』  

『Is that so? If that’s true, that’s somewhat adorable. It’s not the same as with Ain, though; is adorable the right word?』  

『It should be, I guess?』

It’s not as if the word ‘adorable’ was made just to describe me, so it’s not an issue to use it on other people. Though since Ciel’s ‘adorable’ has been only directed towards me and the spirits up until now, I do feel a bit jealous hearing her use it on someone else. Just a bit.

As this went through my mind, I suddenly noticed that Ciel was giggling.

『Ain is still the most adorable, you know?』  

『That’s… Thank you.』

I feel like an open book; it’s embarrassing. As I was thinking of how to change the topic, I detected a potentially bothersome individual—Alcrei—heading here.  

He’s too far away to see us, but examining his route, there are barely any open seats, so he’s definitely going to reach our location.  

It doesn’t seem like he’s noticed us yet, so we can probably make it if we leave now.

『Alcrei is heading towards our general direction; let’s move.』  

『This Alcrei is one of our classmates, right?』  

『He’s the boy whose thunder sorcery ran out of control during the entrance exam.』  

『I remember now. Yeah, he’s going to be bothersome.』

There’s still one sandwich left, but I’ve eaten enough to fuel me for the afternoon, so I shoved it into our magic pouch to eat at a later time.  

Standing up, I then hide my white hair under my robe to at least disguise its length before carrying my dishes for returning. It seems like the girl in front really doesn’t have any particular business with me, as she just continued eating without paying much attention. Seeing her only halfway through her meal, I could barely hold back a smile.

I could leave without saying anything, but since she did catch Ciel’s interest, I warned her, 「A troublesome person is on the way,」 before walking away.  

She quivered upon hearing my voice but then immediately turned to the entrance and had her eyes wide in surprise.  

After that, she carried her tableware in a rush and followed after me.

Just as Alcrei couldn’t see us from here, she shouldn’t be able to see Alcrei as well, so it must be her eyes that allowed her to notice something amiss.  

Truly convenient eyes she has. Jobs come in a lot of varieties, and I believe hers to be special even among others, but who knows?

As I tried to keep distance when crossing paths with Alcrei, he suddenly raised his voice, saying, 「Ah, you—」 For a moment, I thought he was referring to me, but after verifying through detection, it seemed he was simply facing my direction. Immediately after, I heard a small shriek from behind me; is she, by chance, acquainted with Alcrei?

「Belltina. To think a failure such as you would be in this academy. Well, good luck to you.」

Alcrei said mockingly, which the two lackeys behind him laughed in response, before going away.  

The stalker girl called Belltina shrank back for a moment before hurrying after me. Though at this point, I don’t think there’s any meaning in her following me anymore.  

But since it’s not really a problem if she follows us, I guess this is fine. Personally, I feel like I’m being followed by a stray dog lost at a school. Ciel probably wouldn’t understand the comparison, so I’m keeping this to myself.

『Where shall we go?』  

『The girl is still following behind us, right?』  

『That’s right. She might go away eventually, but there’s no way to tell for sure.』  

『Hmm, we still have free time after this, so why don’t we return to the dorm for now?』  

『I see. She shouldn’t follow us until the 5th floor, and she might even return to her own room as well.』

We have free time next period, but who knows how it is in her case.  

Depending on her schedule, she is unlikely to follow us to the dorm, or so I thought, but she’s apparently going to follow us until the 5th floor..  

The moment she stepped into the elevator with us, I was convinced of this.  

As we left the elevator and reached the 5th floor’s lobby area, she finally spoke up, 「Ah, umm…」

In Palra’s case, I believe she talked to us almost right after she arrived, so this girl might be even more introverted than Palra. Palra didn’t feel that introverted of a person to me, but maybe it’s because she was considerably chatty back then.

「How may I help you?」  

「Umm, Bell’s name is Belltina!」

Betraying her silence up until now, she energetically introduced herself, surprising me; but now that I think about it, there were people like this even back in my old world.

「I’m Ailneige. Then, Belltina, is there something wrong?」  

「T-thank you so much for earlier!」

She bowed so hard I feared that her head might hit the ground.

「No need for that. In the end, you still weren’t able to avoid him, after all.」  

「It’s still better than encountering him while eating lunch…」  

「Incidentally, Belltina, your room is on the 5th floor as well?」  

「Yess… Bell has a lot of magic power, but Bell is terrible with sorcery, so Bell was disowned… In exchange for freedom in this academy, Bell’s family cut ties with Bell…  

But still, since Bell has freedom now, that means Bell can stay indoors as much as Bell wants, so Bell’s room has been perfectly prepared for a life of seclusion!」

She seemed dispirited, but she was quick to cheer up. I can’t exactly say if she’s optimistic or pessimistic. Though it’d be tough talking to her had she not cheered up, so I don’t mind this at all. Anyway, it seems like Belltina will need to find work before she graduates. It’s not relevant to us, but I wish her the best of luck.

「So, why have you been following me for a while now?」  

「U-umm… that’s…」

Belltina fiddled with her index fingers while obviously trying to avert my gaze.  

Wondering if she has something to be guilty about, I shot her a stern glare, and she responded in resignation.

「At first Bell just thought, ‘Wow, there’s someone smaller than Bell; then maybe Bell won’t be bullied by her.’」  

「You secretly followed me to the cafeteria even before that, didn’t you?」  

「Umm, uhh… Bell has never been to the cafeteria before. So Bell thought of following someone else there, but since Bell might get scolded when found out, Bell thought of following someone who probably won’t get angry.」  

『Oh, it sounds like Ain’s suspicion was right.』  

『I didn’t think I’d be right either, but from her tone, she doesn’t appear to be lying.』

If her purpose was to keep watch on us or harm us in secret, there shouldn’t be any reason for Belltina to initiate a conversation with us. Most importantly, when she reacted to Alcrei, she was far too defenseless.

「You seem to have noticed my true capabilities, yet you still thought of following me?」  

「Eh!? Umm… uhh… how…」

Is she wondering how I knew of her ability?

「You looked shocked upon seeing me before, and I also observed magic power gathering at your eyes during then. While prying into one’s Job is a breach of etiquette, I assume you have magic eyes of Mana sight, no?」  

「Uhh… yess, that’s right…」

It was a meek response, but my suspicion was correct, so I’m honestly happy about that.  

Magic Eye User is a rare Job to find. Their abilities vary, such as being able to see the imperceptible, far-sight, and so on, but Jobs with special abilities that express themselves through the use of one’s eyes are described under that umbrella term. The term “magic eyes” brings to mind petrification and entrancement, but I haven’t found any information of such ocular abilities having existed.

「Umm, the sight of such a tight-fitting barrier just caught Bell’s eye, that’s all.」  

「You’re lying, aren’t you?」  

「Uhhh, ummm… yess… Bell was surprised after seeing such an unfathomable barrier, but it also looked so safe…」  

「Are you perhaps scheming something?」  

「No, never, not at all! Bell won’t tell anyone about it! Bell only wants to live a quiet and secluded life!  

But that dream is already… impossible…」

Since she’s apparently forsaken by her family, living a secluded life will surely be difficult. As an artificer, you certainly won’t need much interaction with people, and you probably can seclude yourself to create sorceric tools as needed.  

Still, since this isn’t my problem at all, I simply replied, 「Is that so? Thank you for answering honestly.」

+++

# 166: Palra and Belltina’s First Encounter

When I was about to part ways with Belltina, her belly rumbled loudly, so I asked permission from Ciel to give away the leftover sandwich. As Belltina’s embarrassed expression quickly beamed with happiness, I left for our room, where we then had tea with Mia.  

The next course was Herbology, which wasn’t particularly interesting, and the last class of the day was Combat Training.

As with yesterday, we met up with Palra, but then I felt a small presence behind us.

『So Belltina was enrolled in this course as well.』  

『You’re right. I assumed that she wouldn’t have joined courses unrelated to sorceric tools. Did you see her yesterday, Ain?』  

『She didn’t really catch my interest, so… At the very least, I don’t think she had a good record yesterday.』  

『Well, she does seem to be the sorcerer type…』
